software infrastructure?” serves as a doorway. This question resembles

turning on a flashlight in a dimly lit room. As they describe their tech stack,
not only do you understand the tools they use but also the workflows they
follow, the challenges they might be facing, and the gaps that potentially
exist. It is a springboard that dives more deeply.

As you get that overview, it is then crucial to understand the roadmap by
asking, “Are there future plans or software changes on the horizon?” This
question concerns understanding the direction in which the ship is sailing.
“Are you happy with your current setup, or are you seeking change? If you
are looking for a change, what is the driving needs?” It is about discerning
not just the 'what' but also the 'why'.

Lastly, exploring your past with “Tell me about your experiences in previous
software purchases?” provides context. Have you been successfully
integrated in the past? Were there any nightmares you had encountered?
Your past experiences can offer a template on the do´s and don’ts, giving
you the upper hand to ensure a smoother experience for them. It is also a
valid question to ask if they are now using a competitive solution. It is
important to know about their maturity model and technical landscape, as
well as if and how they fit in.


**Key Takeaway:**

Importance: Recognising technology infrastructure provides clarity on the
potential compatibility and integration challenges.

Reason Behind: Integrating new software solutions is easier when aligned
with existing infrastructures, ensuring minimal disruption.

Typical Questions:

“Can you walk me through your current software infrastructure?”

“Are there future plans or software changes on the horizon?”

“Tell me about your experiences in previous software purchases?”

“How do different teams within your organisation interact with your
current software setup?”

“Are you using any solution in area ____ now?”

“What are some repetitive challenges you face with your current
technology infrastructure?”

“Is there a consensus within the company about the tech tools, or are there
differing opinions?”

“How do you typically handle system downtimes or tech glitches?”

“Have there been instances where you had to pivot from a tool or software
due to unforeseen challenges?”

“What is the training process like when you onboard a new tech product?”


#### 7.4.5 Major Pain: Identifying Pain Points and Opportunities

Understanding a prospective environment is not merely a matter of
comprehending the technical infrastructure or demographics. It delves
deeper, reaching the essence of the challenges that they face. Without
knowing what affects a company, how can a solution be offered? The act
of identifying pain points and opportunities is similar to a doctor diagnosing
a patient – essential, sensitive, and foundational.

Addressing a company’s major pain points is analogous to addressing its
pulse. Every business, irrespective of size, industry, or geography, faces
challenges that hinder growth, limit productivity, or simply make day-to-
day operations difficult. These challenges, often termed as pain points, are
the factors that drive companies to seek external solutions, be it in the form
of software, consultancy, or tools. Therefore, understanding these pain
points is not just beneficial; it is elemental to the very fabric of a successful
sales process. (Cohan 2022)

We envision this using a simple analogy. Suppose you are trying to sell a
boat. If you do not know that your prospect has a lake they want to
traverse, you might pitch the boat as a luxury item or leisure product.
However, if you are aware that they have a lake and that they have been
finding it challenging to cross it daily for essential tasks, suddenly, your boat
will transform. It is no longer just an item of luxury; it has become a
necessity and a solution to a tangible problem. This is the power to
understand the pain points.

Why is it vital to directly address these issues? The answer lies in the
tangible value that it offers. Every company seeks solutions that provide
significant value. When you, as a PreSales professional, align your solution
directly with the challenges a company faces, it stops being just a software
or tool. It becomes a tangible asset, a beacon of hope, and a direct response
to a pressing concern. It evolves from being an 'option' to being the
'answer’ '. (Cohan 2022)

Moreover, this alignment does another essential thing. This cements the
relevance and utility of your software offerings. In today’s crowded
marketplace, where every software is claimed to be revolutionary,
groundbreaking, or state-of-the-art, its relevance differentiates one from
the other. By showing that your software directly addresses and resolves
the company’s pain points, you exhibit its utility and unique value
proposition. This is the difference between being 'one of the options' and
'the best option'.

A concrete way to unearth these points of pain is through enquiry. Probing
questions is key to unlocking this treasure trove of information. A
foundational question like, "In your current processes, what challenges do
you face consistently?" is an opener. This provides the prospect of an
opportunity to share, vent, and elucidate. As they describe their challenges,
you get a clear picture of what affects them, allowing you to align your
solutions accordingly. (Cohan 2022)

Taking it a step further, by asking, "If you could redesign certain aspects of
your workflow for the better, what would that be?" You tap into their
aspirations. It is not just about understanding what is wrong now but also
about discerning what they wish for the future. This provides a twofold
advantage. First, it provides insights into the potential upgrades or
improvements that they are considering, allowing you to pitch your
solution as a bridge to that future. Second, it shows the prospect that you
are not only interested in selling a product but also genuinely invested in
their long-term success.

Besides identifying each pain point that your client has, it is important to
grasp how significant these issues are to them. Try to determine what the
problem is worth. Is there a specific deadline for when they aim to fix these

issues? This helps tailor the approach to meet their exact needs and
timelines.


**Key Takeaway:**

Importance: Addressing the prospect's major pain points directly relates to
the tangible value your solution can bring.

Reason Behind: By pinpointing and resolving these issues, you can cement
the relevance and utility of your software offering.

Typical Questions:

“In your current processes, what challenges do you face consistently?”

“If you could redesign certain aspects of your workflow for the better, what
would it be?”

"What has been the financial or operational impact of these challenges?"

"Are there challenges you have faced that have now become the 'norm'
here?"

"What solutions have you previously tried or considered?"

"How do these pain points affect your team’s morale and productivity?"

"If there was one pain point you could eliminate instantly, which would it
be?"


#### 7.4.6 Extended Environment: Broadening the Scope

The primary challenge a company often faces is just the tip of the iceberg,
with a vast array of related issues lurking beneath the surface. Recognising
this interconnected web as a PreSales professional is crucial. It not only
allows a deeper understanding of a company’s challenges but also offers
opportunities to magnify the value of the solution being presented.

Imagine the dynamics of a bustling kitchen in a high-end restaurant. If the
oven starts malfunctioning, it is not just baking that is affected. The entire
workflow, from appetisers to the main course, feels the heat, figuratively
and literally. Orders get delayed, clients grow restless, and chefs feel
pressured. Here, malfunctioning of the ovens is the primary issue.

However, the cascading effects it sets off – delayed orders, disgruntled
clients, and stressed kitchen staff – are adjacent pain points that ripple out
from that central problem. Now, consider the business of selling state-of-
the-art kitchen equipment. Addressing the ovens’ issues is a start, but
showcasing how your solution can improve the kitchen workflow amplifies
its value manifold.

This interconnected nature of business challenges emphasises the
significance of understanding the primary pain points and the extended
environment. Recognising related areas of pain or adjacent issues can be
the difference between offering a patch-up job and delivering a holistic
solution. It can transform your pitch from a band-aid to a comprehensive
remedy. Moreover, this broader perspective provides a crucial edge in a
competitive sales world. (Cohan 2022)

The reason for this broadened scope is rooted in the intertwined nature of
business operations. Rarely does a process or function operate in isolation.
When one gear in a machine grinds to a halt, the entire apparatus
experiences strain. In a business context, this means that a challenge in one
department or function often affects others. It is this domino effect, where
one issue leads to another, that needs to be recognised and addressed. In
doing so, the value of the solution being offered is not confined to solving
one problem. It is considered a panacea for a range of interconnected
challenges.

However, how does one uncover these related areas of pain? As with most
things in PreSales, the answer lies in asking the correct questions. Beginning
with a query like, "Apart from the primary issues we discussed, are there
related areas feeling the strain?" is a door opener. It invites the prospect of
venturing beyond the obvious, shedding light on the challenges that might
be on the periphery but are still impactful.

To delve deeper, consider asking, "How do these adjacent pain points
impact your larger business objectives?" This query serves a dual purpose.
First, it offers insight into the broader ramifications of these related issues.
Furthermore, it subtly positions your solution as not just a problem fix but
also as a catalyst for broader business objectives.


**Key Takeaway:**

Importance: Understanding areas related to pain can uncover additional
avenues for your solution to be beneficial.

Reason Behind: Often, the primary issue has a domino effect on other
processes. Addressing interconnected problems can amplify the perceived
value of a solution.

Typical Questions:

“Apart from the primary issues we discussed, are there related areas feeling
the strain?”

“How do these adjacent pain points impact your larger business
objectives?”

"How do these related challenges affect your teams’ daily operations?"

"Are there processes that get bottlenecked due to these issues?"

"Has the company tried to address these interconnected challenges
before? If so, how?"

"In an ideal scenario, how would you envision these processes working?"

"Are there stakeholders outside of this department who are affected by
these challenges?"


#### 7.4.7 Culture: Navigating Company Dynamics

At its core, company culture is the collective set of values, beliefs,
behaviours, and norms that define an organisation. Shared ethos gives a
company its unique identity, shaping its internal dynamics and external
interactions. From how employees collaborate on projects to how leaders
make decisions, company culture has a say in it. However, in addition to
influencing internal operations, it plays a crucial role in how companies
approach external changes, especially when it comes to adopting new
systems or technologies.

Imagine two companies. Company A has a culture that embraces change,
encourages experimentation, and values innovation. Company B, on the
other hand, is more traditional, valuing tried-and-tested methods over

new-fangled innovations. Now, if you were introducing a cutting-edge
software solution, which company would you think would be more
receptive to? The answer is clear. Company A, with its culture of openness
and innovation, was more likely to welcome this change. Conversely,
Company B, rooted in traditional ways, might be more hesitant or even
resistant.

This brings us to the crux of this matter. Understanding a company’s culture
is not only about gauging its receptiveness to a new solution. It is about
ensuring that your solution aligns seamlessly with a company’s cultural
dynamics. Misalignments can cause trouble. Even the most innovative,
efficient, and cost-effective solution can falter if it clashes with a company-
ingrained way of work. It might face resistance from employees, be
underutilised or worse, and be abandoned entirely. (Cohan 2022)

But why is this so? Why would a company resist solutions that promise
efficiency and growth? The answer lies in inherent human resistance to
change. We are creatures of our habits. We find comfort in the familiar;
anything challenging this status quo can be met with scepticism. This is
amplified in a corporate setting, where established processes and systems
have existed for years and sometimes even decades. The introduction of a
new solution disrupts this equilibrium. If this disruption clashes with a
company’s cultural ethos, it is bound to face hurdles.

For instance, consider a company that values decentralised decision-
making, where teams are empowered to make choices. Introducing a
software solution that centralises control and decision-making might not
sit well. Even if the software promises efficiency, it clashes with the
fundamental cultural tenet of the organisation. The result? Resistance,
scepticism, and a steep uphill battle for adoption.

As PreSales professionals, navigating these cultural waters with finesse is
paramount. The first step in this direction is understanding. Asking
questions like, "How does your company typically approach new software
adoptions?" provides insights into past experiences, successes, and
challenges. It sheds light on a company’s openness to change, its preferred
methods of adoption, and potential roadblocks.

Delving deeper, posing a question like, "Are there predefined methods or
steps your teams follow during such transitions?" offers a window into the
structured approaches that a company might have in place. It reveals the
degree of formalisation in the adoption processes and highlights potential
touchpoints that need to be addressed.

But do not stop there. To truly understand a company’s cultural dynamics,
we broaden the line of enquiry:

"Who are the primary stakeholders in software adoption decisions?"

"Can you share an instance where a new software adoption went
exceptionally well or faced significant challenges?"

"How do you ensure that teams across the organisation are aligned during
such transitions?"

"Are there cultural or organisational values that you believe are non-
negotiable when it comes to new system integrations?"

"How do you handle resistance or scepticism when introducing new
systems or processes?"

Understanding the answers to these questions equips PreSales
professionals with the knowledge to tailor their pitch, ensuring that the
solution aligns with the company’s cultural ethics. It is not just about
showcasing the technical merits of the software but also demonstrating its
cultural compatibility.


**Key Takeaway:**

Importance: Each company’s unique culture influences its adoption and
integration of new systems.

Reason Behind: A solution that does not align with a company’s cultural
dynamics might face resistance or underutilisation.

Typical Questions:

“How does your company typically approach new software adoptions?”

“Are there predefined methods or steps your teams follow during such
transitions?”

"Who are the primary stakeholders in software adoption decisions?"

"Can you share an instance where a new software adoption went
exceptionally well or faced significant challenges?"

"How do you ensure that teams across the organisation are aligned during
such transitions?"

"Are there cultural or organisational values that you believe are non-
negotiable when it comes to new system integrations?"

"How do you handle resistance or scepticism when introducing new
systems or processes?"


#### 7.4.8 Vision Wrap-up: Clarifying the Way Forward

When one navigates the maze of business needs, challenges, and solutions,
getting mired in the details becomes easy. Conversations can become a
whirlwind of technical specifics, challenges, and potential solutions.
However, what sets the trajectory for a successful partnership is not just
the identification of these details but also the alignment of overarching
goals. This is where vision wrap-up comes into play.

Vision wrap-up is a crucial element of PreSales conversations. This is not
merely a recap of what has been discussed. Instead, it is a confirmation that
you have deeply understood clients’ needs. This shows that the solutions
perfectly align with their challenges. Moreover, it is a forward-looking plan.
It crystallises the essence of your discussion, highlighting how your
solutions intertwine with the client’s problems. However, it is not just
about the present; it also sketches a future scenario, illustrating the
positive changes and outcomes that await. This is not just repeating what
was said; it is about showing the path forward. (Cohan 2022)

Understanding the 'why' behind this approach unravels its true
significance. PreSales professionals ensure mutual understanding of their
prospects by wrapping up with a vision. This ensures that both parties have
a shared perspective on the current challenges, proposed solutions, and
potential outcomes. This mutual understanding is foundational. It

minimises miscommunication, sets clear expectations, and paves the way
for effective subsequent engagements. (Cohan 2022)

Moreover, it does something even more profoundly. It catalyses optimism.
By projecting a forward-looking vision, PreSales professionals are not just
selling a product or solution but a brighter future. You are offering a
glimpse into a world in which current challenges are mitigated, if not
eliminated, and business processes are optimised. This aspirational
perspective can be incredibly persuasive as it taps into the innate human
desire for improvement and growth.

For instance, asking a prospect, "Considering the challenges we discussed,
what do you foresee if no changes are made?" is not only about gauging
the gravity of the problem. It prompts introspection, making the prospect
visualise the repercussions of inaction. This underscores the urgency of the
situation, making the need for a solution substantial.

On the other hand, inquiring, "What events or triggers will signify that the
proposed solution is delivering its value?" shifts the lens towards positive
outcomes. It encourages the prospect to envision success and imagine a
scenario where challenges are tackled efficiently, thanks to the proposed
solution. This creates a vivid mental image of success that can be a potent
motivator.

Lastly, rounding off with a question like, "Shall we outline the next steps to
ensure synchronized efforts moving forward?" is a masterstroke. It is
proactive, signalling commitment and eagerness. It shows the prospect
that you are not just there to make a sale but are genuinely invested in their
success. It transforms the conclusion from being an end to a conversation
into the beginning of a partnership.

In the broader landscape of business engagement, it is easy to
underestimate the power of conclusions. However, every nuance counts in
the world of PreSales, where the stakes are high and competition is fierce.
A vision wrap-up is one such nuance that can make all the difference.

Essentially, this is about crafting a narrative. A narrative where the
prospective challenges are acknowledged, solutions are provided, and a
brighter future is projected. It resonates with the prospect's aspirations,

aligning with their goals and charting out a path to achieve them together.
(Cohan 2022)

As PreSales professionals, the objective is not just to offer a product or
service. It is about offering a partnership and a journey towards mutual
success. Furthermore, the vision wrap-up is the compass that points the
way.


**Key Takeaway:**

Importance: Concluding a vision wrap-up ensures alignment between
prospect expectations and your offerings. It also sets the tone for
subsequent engagement.

Reason Behind: Establishing a clear path ensures that both parties are on
the same page, thereby optimising the chances of successful collaboration.

Typical Questions:

“Considering the challenges we discussed, what do you foresee if no
changes are made?”

“What events or triggers will signify that the proposed solution is delivering
its value?”

“Shall we outline the next steps to ensure synchronized efforts moving
forward?”


### 7.5 Techniques for Effective Discovery

The discovery phase, a cornerstone of the PreSales process, is similar to
peeling an onion. Layer-by-layer, it is about delving deeper, uncovering
nuances, and identifying the core. To facilitate this exploration, PreSales
professionals need a set of techniques in their arsenal, each offering a
unique perspective, each shining a light on a different facet of the
prospect's needs, challenges, and aspirations.

Researching the company at the beginning of the discovery phase is crucial.
Nowadays, there's a wealth of information available on the internet about
any company. This research provides a solid foundation, enabling you to
ask informed questions and demonstrate a deep understanding of the

prospect’s business from the outset. More importantly, if you have done
proper research before, you can drop in a few pieces of information you
have gathered. For example: “I have seen you have increased your revenue
by 10%; what impact does this have on the operation?”

One of the most potent techniques at the disposal of PreSales professionals
is the use of open-ended questions. But what exactly is an open-ended
question? At its heart, it is an invitation. It is an invitation for the prospect
to share, elaborate, and dive into the intricacies of challenges and needs.
Unlike closed-ended questions, which often lead to monosyllabic answers
such as “yes” or “no”, open-ended questions pave the way for more
detailed responses. For instance, rather than merely asking if a prospect
faces challenges with its software, nudging them to describe those
challenges offers a wealth of insights. It is not just about identifying the
existence of a problem but also about understanding its depth,
implications, and ripple effects. (Cohan 2022)

Asking comparative questions, such as how the current year's performance
aligns with the previous year or their initial expectations, can reveal
underlying trends, shifts in priorities, and deeper insights into their
operational challenges and strategic goals. This approach helps to
contextualize their experiences and offers a richer understanding of their
trajectory and aspirations.

The SPIN technique is a structured method that enhances discovery by
breaking down the conversation into four key components: Situation,
Problem, Implication, and Need-Payoff. Start by exploring the current
situation to understand the context in which the business operates. Next,
identify specific problems they face, delve into the implications of these
issues, and discuss the potential payoffs from solving them. This technique
guides the conversation smoothly from problem identification to proposing
compelling solutions.

During discussions, aim to uncover not just the superficial challenges but
also the broader impact these issues have on the customer's operations.
Understanding their critical pain points — what truly keeps them up at
night — enables you to tailor your solutions to their most urgent needs,
thereby positioning your offering as both strategic and indispensable.

While asking the right questions is half the battle, truly comprehending the
answers is the other half. Strategic use of silence after posing a question
can be incredibly effective. It gives clients the space to think and articulate
their thoughts fully, often leading them to share more insights than
planned. This can be particularly valuable in uncovering deeper truths
about their situation and needs. Active listening plays an indispensable role
in this process. Active listening is not a passive absorption; it is an engaged,
attentive, and conscious effort to grasp the spoken words and the
emotions, concerns, and sentiments that lace them. When a prospect
articulates a concern, taking a moment to summarise and reflect on it
shows that one has been attentive and offers an opportunity to clarify any
ambiguities. This strengthens the bridge of understanding between both
parties, ensuring that subsequent solutions are rooted in a clear
comprehension of the issues at hand. (Rosenberg 2015)

Empathy, often hailed as one of the most crucial traits in sales, finds
structured expression in empathy mapping. An empathy map is more than
just a tool; it is also a perspective. It is about slipping on the prospect’s
shoes, seeing the world through their eyes, and feeling their challenges
viscerally. This technique provides a comprehensive understanding of the
prospect's emotional landscape by breaking down feedback into distinct
sections like what the client 'Says', 'Feels', 'Does', and 'Thinks'. Such insights
are invaluable; they offer a human touch on the solutions proposed,
ensuring they resonate emotionally as much as they do logically.

SWOT analysis is a key tool for understanding the prospective business
landscape in a structured and comprehensive manner. It is a navigational
aid that helps identify where the prospect excels and where they have
opportunities to capitalise on. At the same time, it sheds light on the
weaknesses and potential risks they might face. For instance, recognising a
client’s position as a market leader is crucial as it is a significant strength.
However, it is just as important to be aware of the challenges that they may
encounter, such as regulatory hurdles. This complete view is vital because
it ensures that the solutions we offer are not only effective but also well-
rounded. They address a wide range of issues while also creating most of
the opportunities. (Hungenberg 2014)

However, the identification of a challenge is sometimes insufficient. One
must trace its roots, delve into its genesis, and understand its core
structure. This is where the '5 Whys' technique shines. By repeatedly asking
'why', it peels back the layers, each time going a step deeper until the
foundational cause emerges. This transforms superficial understanding
into profound insights. If sales are declining because of unhappy clients and
those clients are discontented because of software glitches, addressing the
software issue can resolve the overarching sales challenge. (Cohan 2022;
Greene 2018; Keenan 2018)


**Key Takeaway:**

Open-Ended Questions
Definition: Questions that cannot be answered with a simple "yes" or "no",
encouraging the prospect to elaborate.

Example: Instead of asking, "Do you face challenges with your current
software?" ask, "Can you describe the challenges you experience with your
current software?" (Rackham 1995)

Active Listening
Definition: Listening with full attention, ensuring that you are not just
hearing the words but grasping the underlying sentiments and concerns.

Example: After a prospect explains a pain point, summarize it by saying,
"So, if I understand correctly, your main concern is..."

Empathy Mapping
Definition: A tool to help understand a prospect's emotions, needs, and
challenges. It is about putting oneself in prospect's shoes.

Example: Breaking down a client’s feedback into sections like 'Says', 'Feels',
'Does', and 'Thinks'.

SWOT Analysis
Definition: Analysing the prospect's Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities,
and Threats to obtain a holistic understanding of the business environment.

Example: Identifying potential client market leadership as a strength but
recognising regulatory challenges as a weakness.

The 5 Whys
Definition: A technique to get to the root cause of a problem by asking
'why' multiple times.

Example: "Why are sales declining?" "Because clients are unhappy." "Why
are clients unhappy?" "Because the software is glitchy."


### 7.6 Common Challenges in Discovery

The art of discovery in PreSales is the dance of subtle nuances, probing
questions, and dedicated listening. It is a space where PreSales
professionals seek to uncover a potential client’s deepest challenges,
needs, and aspirations. However, like any intricate dance, this process does
not come without a fair share of missteps and stumbling blocks. While the
intention is always to build a bridge of understanding, professionals often
encounter challenges that threaten to disrupt this connection.

First on the list of these challenges is the encounter with surface-level
information. Picture this: You are in a crucial discovery meeting, and as you
ask probing questions, hoping to get to the heart of clients’ challenges, you
receive answers that are generic or superficial. Such answers are like masks,
concealing the real issues underneath them. Instead of an in-depth view of
the intricacies of their problems, you get a panoramic shot, wide but lacking
in depth. This can be frustrating for PreSales professionals. Without
understanding the detailed landscape of clients’ challenges, crafting
tailored solutions becomes a daunting task. The risk here is proposing
solutions that may appear disconnected or irrelevant to the prospect’s core
needs, leading to lost opportunities or prolonged sales cycles. (Cohan 2022)

A close cousin of surface-level information is defensiveness, which is
another frequent challenge. It is not uncommon for clients to approach
discovery sessions cautiously. Their defences are up, and there is an
underlying hesitation to share too much. This wariness often stems from a
fear of being "sold to" or pushed into a corner with a sales pitch. In such
instances, the flow of information becomes a trickle, making it difficult for
PreSales professionals to gauge real issues and, consequently, design

effective solutions. It is akin to navigating a maze in a dim light – every turn
becomes uncertain, and the path to success is convoluted.

Then, there is the challenge of misalignment, which is a tricky terrain for
navigation. Companies, especially larger ones, are comprised of multiple
stakeholders, each bringing a unique perspective to the table. One
department might view a particular software limitation as the primary
challenge, while another might believe that the real issue lies in workflow
inefficiency. Such divergent views could muddy the water of discovery. The
danger here is twofold: not only is there a risk of missing out on critical
challenges by focusing on just one perspective, but there is also the
potential of proposing solutions that might be favoured by one stakeholder
but opposed by another. In such scenarios, consensus becomes elusive and
moving forward becomes a game of balancing diverse viewpoints.

Finally, time constraints can cast a formidable shadow over the discovery
process. Time is a valuable commodity, and not all prospects can allocate
generous chunks of it to discovery sessions. You may be looking for quick
answers or solutions, often at the expense of depth and thoroughness. This
rush against the clock can pressure PreSales professionals, leading to
potential oversights or hasty conclusions. When discovery is rushed, there
is a heightened risk of missing subtle but critical details, which can later
manifest as gaps in the proposed solution.

While these challenges might seem daunting, recognising them is the first
step towards devising strategies to effectively navigate them. The beauty
of the PreSales domain lies in its dynamism and the opportunity it offers
professionals to innovate, adapt, and overcome it. By developing a toolkit
of techniques, fostering genuine client relationships, and cultivating a keen
sense of observation, PreSales professionals can transform these
challenges into opportunities for growth.

The discovery phase, which is filled with potential stumbling blocks, is
worth undertaking. Challenges, although significant, were not impossible
to overcome. With the right approach, patience, and a touch of ingenuity,
PreSales professionals can not only navigate these challenges but turn
them into stepping stones towards deeper understanding and more robust
solutions. After all, in the dance of discovery, every misstep is a lesson,

every challenge is an invitation to innovate, and every solution is a
testament to the enduring spirit of the PreSales profession. (Cohan 2022)


**Key Takeaway:**

Surface-Level Information: Prospects may initially provide generic or
surface-level answers.

Defensiveness: Some clients may be wary of sharing too much, fearing a
sales pitch.

Misalignment: Different stakeholders may have different views on
challenges and needs.

Time Constraints: Prospects might be unwilling to dedicate ample time to
discovery.


### 7.7 Overcoming Discovery Challenges

A good place to start is to build trust. The hesitation that we encounter
from prospects during discovery often stems from a fundamental lack of
trust. They may be wary of past experiences or a natural inclination to
guard company secretions. They might be wondering: "Is this just another
sales gimmick? Is the end goal merely to make a sale?" It is essential to
dispel these doubts early. Trust is the foundation of any fruitful interaction.
The intention behind the discovery process is not merely to make a sale but
to genuinely provide value and offer a solution that addresses potential
challenges. Trust is cultivated by demonstrating genuine interest in the
prospective challenges, listening more than speaking, and ensuring
transparency in every interaction. When the prospect senses this genuine
intent, they are likelier to let down their guard and engage in meaningful
conversation. (Cohan 2022)

The B2B scenarios further complicate the discovery landscape. In such
cases, decisions are rarely unilateral. Multiple stakeholders come into play,
each bringing their perspective, challenges, and priorities to the table.
Engaging all of these stakeholders is crucial. Imagine trying to solve a jigsaw
puzzle using only half of the pieces. The picture remains incomplete.

Similarly, by only engaging with a fraction of the decision-makers, we risk
missing a holistic understanding of the challenges and needs. It is essential
to recognise the multifaceted nature of B2B decisions and ensure that our
discovery process encompasses all these perspectives. By engaging
multiple stakeholders, we gather a comprehensive view, ensuring that our
proposed solutions resonate with broader organisational goals and not just
individual viewpoints.

Flexibility is another crucial aspect of navigating discovery challenges. This
trait allows us to pivot when facing unexpected hurdles. Prospects may be
tight on time, wary of deep dives, or prefer to have a demo in the first
meeting. The strictness of our approach can be counterproductive. If a
prospect is more comfortable with multiple, shorter discovery sessions, it
might be beneficial to accommodate this preference. Alternatively, if a line
of questioning seems to place them on the edge, a change in direction could
be more fruitful. Adaptability, in essence, ensures that we are not just
following a set script but are genuinely engaged in a conversation, reading
the room, and adjusting our sails based on the wind of our prospects’
comfort. (Cohan 2022)

Finally, while we can vouch for the value of a thorough discovery process,
sometimes it helps to let our past successes do the talking. This is where
testimonials and case studies have come into play. Real-world examples of
how a detailed discovery process leads to successful outcomes are
persuasive. These narratives serve two purposes. First, we provide tangible
evidence of the benefits of deep engagement in the discovery process.
Second, you offer a glimpse of the potential benefits awaiting them on the
other side of a thorough discovery. Essentially, it acts as a bridge to trust,
connecting past successes with future potential.


**Key Takeaway:**

Building Trust: Ensure that the prospect knows that the intent is to provide
value, not just make a sale.

Engaging All Stakeholders: In B2B scenarios, multiple decision-makers are
engaged to obtain a comprehensive view.

Flexible Approach: Be willing to adapt based on the prospects’ comfort,
whether this means multiple shorter sessions or changing the line of
questioning.

Leverage Testimonials: Use case studies or testimonials to show the value
of a thorough discovery process.


### 7.8 Translating Discovery into Value Propositions

The art of PreSales is not merely about uncovering the challenges or
understanding the operational landscape of a potential client. It is about
bridging the gap between these challenges and the unique value of
solutions. Think of the discovery process as a meticulous mining act:
extracting raw gems from depths. Translating this discovery into value
propositions is the art of cutting and polishing these gems and turning them
into sparkling jewels ready to be showcased.

After a robust discovery session, a PreSales professional is armed with
invaluable insights into the prospect’s operations, challenges, and
aspirations. This information represents the raw materials. The next critical
step is to mould this material into a compelling narrative that underscores
the tangible value of the solution. (Cohan 2022)

We begin with the alignment of the solutions to the pain points. Imagine a
scenario in which a prospect outlines challenges in real-time data analytics
due to outdated software. It is insufficient to present a state-of-the-art
analytical tool for your offering. Instead, the emphasis should be on how
this tool was designed to counter these challenges. The focus should shift
from what the tool does on a general level to how it provides a solution
tailored to its unique problem. For instance, if the latency in data
processing is a pain point, it emphasises how the software eliminates this
lag, ensuring real-time data processing. By making these direct connections
between challenges and solutions, the value proposition becomes crystal-
clear to the prospect. They no longer see a tool; they see a solution.

However, understanding the solution is one thing and grasping its tangible
impact is another. This is where Return on Investment (ROI) comes into
play. In a business environment, numbers often speak louder than words
do. Prospects do not just want to know how your solution addresses their

pain points; they also want to understand the economic implications of
adopting your solution. Craft a potential ROI model based on discovery-
phase insights. For instance, if a prospective challenge revolves around
inefficient client service leading to loss of clients, demonstrate how your
solution can increase efficiency, potentially reduce client attrition, and
increase revenue. Present these in tangible metrics: enhanced client
satisfaction scores, reduction in service time, or potential revenue upticks.
Such numerical representation makes the value proposition concrete,
allowing prospects to envision the financial benefits of partnering with you.

Having established the solution alignment and potential ROI, it is now time
to bring this value proposition to life. Enter-tailored Product Demos. A
generic demonstration of features is similar to a broad brushstroke on a
canvas, but what you aim for is a detailed masterpiece. Given the rich
insights gained from the discovery phase, your demonstration should
mirror all this information. Instead of showcasing a plethora of features,
focus is placed on functionalities that directly resonate with the prospect’s
context. If a prospect highlights the challenges in data visualisation, ensure
that your demo emphasises this aspect of your product. Moreover, using
real-world scenarios, perhaps even simulating some of the challenges
discussed during discovery, will showcase how your solution elegantly
navigates these issues. Such a tailored demonstration not only reinforces
the relevance of your solution but also provides prospects for a glimpse into
a world where their challenges are mitigated, if not eliminated. (Cohan
2022)


**Key Takeaway:**

Align Solutions with Pain Points: Clearly demonstrate how your offering
addresses the specific challenges highlighted during discovery.

Showcase ROI: Based on the identified challenges and objectives, potential
ROIs are calculated and presented.

Craft Tailored Demos: Utilize insights from discovery to tailor product
demonstrations that resonate with the prospect’s unique context.


### 7.9 Doing a Demo in a Discovery

“Never ever do a Demo without Discovery (Never?)”

We in PreSales have this paradigm that we do not execute demos (and you
should never do that) without proper discovery. However, what are you
doing if your Sales Partner promises it or if the client wants to see
something?

The dance between PreSales and Sales is delicate choreography. It must
move in harmony, guiding potential clients across the floor of
understanding and towards the ultimate goal of partnership. However,
sometimes, the steps can become out of sync, especially when a product
demo is promised amidst a discovery session. For those in PreSales, the
idea of diving into a demonstration without the foundation of
comprehensive discovery can be disconcerted. However, as with many
aspects of business, flexibility and adaptability are crucial. (Cohan 2022)

Imagine a scenario: your sales partner passionately clinches a potential lead
and has promised a sneak peek into the product. Alternatively, perhaps the
client, driven by curiosity, has expressed an eager desire to "see" the
solution before diving deep into their challenges. This might seem like a
hazardous position, especially for PreSales professionals who firmly believe
in the holiness of the discovery process. However, if navigated thoughtfully,
this situation can become an opportunity. Thinking about the Give-Get
Framework.

While audience anticipation is at its zenith, capitalises on this excitement.
Begin with a crisp pitch and broad paintings of the solution potential. This
is not the time for minute details but for sharing the grand vision. A visual
demonstration can be particularly effective. By using compelling visuals,
the audience gets a birds-eye view of what to expect, satiating their
immediate curiosity without delving into intricate details.

This preliminary showcase should be brief – ideally, not more than 5–10
min. Following this, one might venture into what some industry veterans
call a 'Look & Feel Demo'. The essence here is not to provide an exhaustive
walkthrough but to offer a flavour of the system’s ambience. Think of it as
offering a trailer rather than an entire movie. Highlighting navigational
ease, showcasing captivating dashboards, or perhaps illustrating a simple
use case can be effective. The aim is to determine appetite, making the
prospect eager for a more comprehensive exploration in subsequent
engagements.

However, the challenge lies in ensuring that this brief demo does not
inadvertently deviate from a deep dive. As the navigator of this journey,
the PreSales professional must resist the allure of the "rabbit hole". It is
natural for a curious prospect to proceed further; however, it is crucial to
steer them back to the path of discovery. If the conversation begins to veer
deeply into specifics, acknowledging the enquiry is an artful skill while
promising a more thorough examination after a comprehensive discovery.
(Cohan 2022)

The silver lining in this approach is the unique opportunity it presents to
conduct a discovery within the demo. As you illustrate, features or
functionalities intersperse the demo with probing questions. This keeps the
prospect engaged and aids in gaining insights about their needs and
challenges in real-time.

This approach requires a certain level of skill and confidence. Balancing the
act of presenting a product effectively while gathering critical insights from
a client is not an easy task. It demands confidence, articulation of
communication, and quick thinking. For those new to the PreSales role, it
is wise to approach this method with caution. Start slowly, learn from each
experience, and gradually build your expertise. Over time, as you gain more
experience and confidence, this strategy will become an essential and
powerful tool for your professional toolkit. It is all about growing and
adapting with each interaction and learning opportunity.

Providing additional resources is a great strategy if the prospect still seeks
more information after a brief demo. Think of these appetisers that set the
stage for the main course, which is a detailed demonstration.
Supplementary materials such as brochures, whitepapers, and automated
demos can provide prospects with a sneak peek into the full capabilities of
your solution. They help build anticipation and interest, offering a broader
understanding of what is in. These resources are not just informative; they
are strategic tools to maintain engagement and interest, leading to a more
comprehensive demonstration of the product.


### 7.10 How to learn doing discovery

Discovery is the bedrock of effective PreSales. Through the discovery
process, PreSales professionals unearthed the intricate details of potential

client challenges, objectives, and expectations. Mastery in this art is crucial
to understanding the prospect's needs and tailoring a solution that aligns
seamlessly with your requirements. How does one cultivate this essential
skill?

I strongly recommend that anyone who wants to become a PreSales
professional reads the book "Doing Discovery." It is a very helpful book on
this topic, and it helps readers fully understand all the details involved in
discovery. This book has discussed some aspects of discovery, but "Doing
Discovery" goes into more detail and sheds light on important and
complicated parts. It goes into great detail about the ideas we have
touched upon and introduces many new advanced techniques and
strategies. Reading this book is a must if you want to really understand the
depth of discovery. (Cohan 2022)

Like many other skills, mastering the art of discovery goes beyond
theoretical knowledge. Understanding concepts and reading them is just
the starting point. True expertise in discovery comes from hands-on
practice and real-world experience. It is similar to learning to swim; you
cannot become proficient simply by reading about swimming techniques.
You need to get into the water, feel resistance, try out different strokes,
and continuously refine your technique based on your experiences.
Similarly, the practice of discovery requires actively engaging in
conversations, asking questions, listening, and learning from each
interaction to truly hone their skills. Through this practical application, the
nuances and subtleties of effective discovery are understood and
mastered.

Begin with mock sessions. Engage colleagues or sales partners in simulated
discovery exercises. Such controlled environments allow for mistakes,
corrections, feedback, and improvements without the pressure of actual
client interactions. Consider these sessions as safe playgrounds where
every stumble is an opportunity to refine the technique. Jordan Belfort,
known as the "Wolf of Wall Street," emphasizes the importance of
structured practice and mock sessions to master sales techniques. His
approach can be highly effective for conducting discovery sessions in the
pre-sales process. Implementing a structured flow during discovery
sessions can significantly enhance your effectiveness. This involves

systematically gathering information about the prospect, their team,
workflows, and current environment. Understanding their major pain
points and envisioning potential improvements are key steps in this
process. Belfort’s methodology emphasizes the importance of following a
consistent and logical sequence to uncover the prospect's needs and tailor
your solution accordingly. (Belfort 2020)

The essence of this discovery is conversation. Moreover, like any
conversation, it should flow organically and seamlessly from one topic to
another, with the underlying objective of gleaning insights. This flow makes
the discovery process feel natural and unforced, encouraging the prospect
of open sharing. Train yourself to pose open-ended questions that nudge
the prospect of elaborating and steering the dialogue towards revealing
valuable information. (Cohan 2022)

However, asking questions is just one aspect of the coin. It is equally
important to listen, not just to hear. As you engage in these mock sessions,
hone your active listening skills. Process the shared information,
understand the emotions underlying the words, and frame subsequent
questions based on the insights gathered. I recommend the books by
Marshal Rosenberg.

Feedback is the golden tool in this learning journey. After every mock
session, seek feedback from your colleague or Sales partner. Understand
where you excelled and faltered. Did you manage to keep the conversation
flowing? Were there any moments of awkwardness? Did you delve deep
enough, or did you skim the surface? Using this feedback constructively,
identify areas of improvement and work on them in subsequent sessions.

Recall that discovery is as much about understanding as it is about building
a relationship. It is about fostering trust, showcasing genuine interest in the
prospect's challenges, and positioning yourself not merely as a seller but as
a partner who is invested in their success.

As you keep practising, you will see a noticeable boost in your confidence.
The early hesitations and nerves you might have felt will start to diminish,
giving way to a new sense of assurance and poise. As this happens, you find
that your questioning becomes more fluid and spontaneous. Your ability to
listen will sharpen and become more intuitive and focused. In turn, this

deepens the quality of conversations. You will be able to engage more
meaningfully with prospects, understand their needs and challenges more
profoundly, and offer solutions that are closely aligned with their goals. This
growing confidence and skill set will not only make your interactions more
effective but also more rewarding for both you and your clients.

However, the journey of mastering the discoveries does not end. The
business landscape is dynamic, and with this, the challenges and needs of
the prospects evolve. Stay updated, keep refining your skills, and always be
open to learning. In PreSales, discovery is not just a one-time activity; it is
a continuous journey of understanding, adapting, and delivering
unmatched value.


**Key Takeaway:**

Foundation of Effective PreSales: Discovery is crucial for PreSales
professionals to understand client challenges, objectives, and expectations.
Mastery in discovery allows for solutions that align seamlessly with client
needs.

Mock Sessions for Practice: Begin with mock sessions involving colleagues
or sales partners. These simulated exercises provide a safe environment to
make mistakes, receive feedback, and improve without the pressure of real
client interactions.

Conversational Flow: Discovery should feel like a natural conversation.
Train yourself to ask open-ended questions that encourage prospects to
share valuable information. The goal is to make the process organic and
unforced.

Active Listening: Listening is as important as asking questions. Develop
active listening skills to understand not just the words but also the
emotions behind them. This helps in framing subsequent questions and
gaining deeper insights.

Building Relationships: Discovery is about building trust and showcasing
genuine interest in the prospect's challenges. Position yourself as a partner
invested in their success, not just a seller.


## 8. The Discovery Summary / Opportunity Scoping

Document (OSD)
Picture: You have just had an insightful, engaging discovery session with a
prospect. The dialogue was rich and filled with revelations about prospects’
needs, challenges, and visions. As a PreSales professional, you are
brimming with ideas and strategies to tailor your solutions to these insights.
But as the excitement of the meeting fades, a critical question arises: How
do you retain the essence of this dialogue? How do you ensure that the
myriad details, sentiments, and aspirations discussed are not lost in
translation as you move forward in the sales process?

Enter the Opportunity Scoping Document (OSD), a beacon that illuminates
the path ahead. The OSD is more than just a summary or record at its core.
This demonstrates the mutual understanding and alignment achieved
during the discovery phase. It serves a dual purpose by encapsulating the
essence of discovery dialogue. For the seller, it is a roadmap guiding
subsequent strategies, pitches, and demonstrations. For the client, it is a
testament to the sellers’ commitment, an assurance that their needs and
challenges are understood and will be central to the proposed solutions.

However, what sets an effective OSD apart from a mere transactional
record? How does one craft an OSD that resonates, engages, and ensures?

The Opportunity Scoping Document (OSD) is all about being clear,
thorough, and in sync with clients’ needs. It should clearly capture the
details of your discovery conversations in a way that is easy to understand
and act upon. It does not really matter if it is a written document,
PowerPoint, or summary in a CRM system. Most importantly, it accurately
reflects what was discussed and agreed upon.

A well-crafted OSD begins with a clear structure. It begins by delineating
the objectives of the discovery session and setting the context for the
following insights, followed by a detailed account of the prospects of the
current landscape – their challenges, needs, aspirations, and constraints.
Every pain point discussed and every goal articulated finds a place in this
section, ensuring a comprehensive understanding of the prospect’s world.

Subsequently, the OSD focuses on the proposed solutions. Here, ensuring
that everything aligns with the client’s needs is key. Each solution, strategy,
or suggestion that we offer is directly linked to what we learned about the
client during the discovery phase. In this way, the client does not simply see
a list of generic offerings. Instead, they see customised plans specifically
designed for their unique situation.

Nevertheless, an OSD is not just about looking back but also charting the
path forward. Hence, a well-constructed OSD will also detail the next steps,
timelines, and expectations, ensuring that both parties are aligned in their
journey ahead.

Crafting an OSD requires a blend of meticulousness and empathy. Every
sentiment captured during the discovery phase needs to be woven into the
document with precision. However, it is also essential to step back, view
the OSD from a prospective perspective, and ensure that it resonates with
expectations and aspirations. This blend of objectivity and empathy sets
apart impactful OSD.

However, the OSD journey does not end with its creation. In many
scenarios, sharing an OSD with a prospect is advisable. This fosters
transparency and provides an opportunity to validate the insights captured,
ensuring no misalignment or oversight. When a prospect reviews the OSD,
you are not just revisiting the discovery dialogue; you are validating the
sellers’ understanding and commitment, further strengthening the
foundation of a value-driven relationship.

However, the OSD, even though it can be client-facing, benefits the whole
organisation. Think about Professional Service, which needs to come up
with a Services Estimate, or Product Management, which needs to align
with the gaps. Or you need to present the opportunity to the leadership.
Finally, the document can be used for handover to the implementation
teams.


### 8.1 The Importance of an OSD

Imagine the OSD as a bridge. On the one hand, you have detailed, nuanced
discussions of the discovery phase, brimming with insights, aspirations,
challenges, and concerns. Conversely, the vast landscape of the sales

journey ahead is marked by demos, proposals, negotiations and solutions.
The OSD serves as the key link between these domains, ensuring that the
momentum of the discovery phase is not lost but rather harnessed to
propel the relationship forward.

Testament to Understanding

Every interaction in the PreSales process carries the promise of
understanding. Prospects sharing their worlds’ intricacies and laying bare
their challenges, aspirations, and constraints. This act of sharing is based on
trust and the belief that the PreSales team is not just listening but truly
understanding. The OSD stands as a tangible affirmation of this belief.
(Cohan 2022)

A well-crafted OSD is not merely a summary of what has been discussed. It
is an interpretation, a reflection that the PreSales team has not only heard
but also deeply understood the prospect's narrative. Every detail in the
OSD, from the challenges outlined to the aspirations highlighted, resonates
with the prospects’ voices, assuring them that their story has been
internalised.

By offering this assurance, OSD sets the tone for the relationship. It sends
a clear message: "We have listened, we understand, and we are committed
to tailoring our solutions to your unique context." Doing so lays the
foundation for trust and credibility, which are essential ingredients for a
value-driven partnership.

Foundation for Future Engagements

The sales journey is dynamic and marked by a series of interactions, with
each building on the other. As the relationship progresses, the discussions
become more focused, diving deeper into specific solutions and strategies.
However, what guides these discussions? What ensures that they remain
rooted in the insights and understanding garnered during the discovery
phase?

The answer is the OSD. By capturing the essence of the discovery dialogue,
the OSD serves as a foundational reference for all subsequent
engagements. Be it a detailed product demonstration tailored to the
prospect's challenges or a proposal that aligns with their goals and

constraints, the OSD ensures that these interactions are not isolated events
but are deeply interconnected, each drawing from and building upon the
insights of the previous.

For instance, when demonstrating a feature or solution, referencing the
OSD ensures that the focus remains on how this feature addresses a
specific challenge or aspiration discussed during discovery. This continuity
ensures relevance and reinforces PreSales teams’ commitment to offering
solutions that are truly aligned with the prospects’ needs.

Ensuring Internal Consistency

The world of PreSales is not just about their relationship with prospects.
Internally, coordination and consistency are paramount within a sales
team. Multiple stakeholders, from sales strategists to technical experts,
play a role in shaping sales narratives. In this multifaceted team, how does
one ensure that everyone is singing on the same hymn sheet?

The OSD raises this challenge, acting as a single source of truth for the
entire team. By detailing the prospect requirements, challenges,
expectations, and sentiments, the OSD ensures that every team member,
irrespective of their role in the sales process, is aligned in their
understanding and approach.

Imagine a scenario in which the technical team needs to customise a
solution based on unique prospect challenges. Instead of relying on
fragmented notes or second-hand information, one can refer to the OSD to
gain a clear and comprehensive view of the prospect’s context. This not
only streamlines the customisation process but also guarantees that the
solution remains aligned with the prospect's needs.

The OSD acts as the team’s compass, guiding strategies, approaches, and
solutions, ensuring internal consistency and alignment at every step.


**Key Takeaway:**

A Testament to Understanding: A well-crafted OSD proves that PreSales
has listened to, understood, and aligned with prospect needs.

Foundation for Future Engagements: Every following interaction, be it a
demonstration or proposal, leverages the OSD as a foundational reference.

Ensuring Internal Consistency: Within the organisation, the OSD
guarantees that everyone is on the same page regarding the prospect
requirements, challenges, and expectations.


### 8.2 Structuring the OSD

The following structure can be used, but additional elements can be
developed if business needs require it. The OSD template can be found on
www.presales-handbook.com.

Document History: Think of this as a cover page or a preamble. It is where
you outline the versions of the OSD, capture modification dates, and
identify the contributors. This section ensures that the document's lineage
is preserved as it evolves, allowing all stakeholders to understand its
progression.

Executive Summary: In a few concise paragraphs, offer a snapshot of the
company, illuminate its principal challenges, and suggest how your offering
can be the beacon. This section is crucial as it often sets the tone for the
reader, offering a glimpse of what lies ahead in the document.

Company Profile: A deep dive into the prospect’s organisation. This is more
than just facts and figures. While you will capture essential details such as
company size, industry type, and current solutions in place, you also want
to paint a picture of the organisation’s ethos. Highlight key stakeholders
and organisational structure, and perhaps even touch upon their market
standing. In this section you would add the client map.

Goals, Challenges, and Major Pain Points: This lies bare the heart of the
matter. Detail the issues that the prospect grapples with, delve into the
implications of these challenges, and perhaps postulate the root causes. By
doing so, you will demonstrate your in-depth understanding and set the
stage for your solution. (Cohan 2022)

Desired Outcomes and Vision: Now, pivot the narrative from challenges to
aspirations. Chart out the prospect’s objectives, outline what success looks
like to them, and encapsulate broader business goals. This section radiates
optimism, showcasing the brighter future that your solution promises.
(Cohan 2022)

Supply Chain Map: A graphical or textual representation of prospect
operations illustrating how products or services flow through the
organisation. This aids in understanding bottlenecks, inefficiencies, or
crucial nodes.

IT Overview and Architecture: A synopsis of the prospects of current
technical landscapes. What systems do they employ? How do these
systems communicate with each other? Are there legacy systems that
require special consideration?

Project Prioritisation and Business Releases: Understand and note the
sequence in which the prospect wishes to roll out solutions or address
challenges. This provides a timeline view and aids resource allocation.

Assumptions & Gaps: This key section details our assumptions, ensuring
everyone involved - you, your client, and our internal teams, such as
Professional Service, understand the same thing. This is a protective
measure against future confusion or misunderstandings. Clear
communication helps to keep all parties aligned and informed. (Cohan
2022)

Modules & Detailed Scoping: A deep dive into specific functionalities or
modules of your solution that address the needs of your prospects. Here,
you align features with challenges and craft a narrative of resolution and
relief.

Meeting Notes: A repository of discussions, decisions, and revelations.
However, more than just a log, this section should be structured to highlight
action items, responsibilities, and follow-up. This is the pulse of the OSD,
keeping the sales process alive and dynamic.

Although this structure provides a comprehensive blueprint, it is essential
to understand that not all OSDs are cast from the same mould.
Organisations vary, industries have nuances, and sales processes are often
as unique as fingerprints. Therefore, this structure was treated as a starting
point and scaffold for constructing the OSD.

Recall that the OSD is more than just a document; it is a narrative. As you
tailor it to fit your unique context, ensure that the narrative flows,
resonates, and most importantly, aligns perfectly with both the vendors’

promises and prospects’ expectations. In PreSales, where understanding is
the currency and alignment is the goal, a well-crafted OSD is the most
potent asset.


### 8.3 Tips for Crafting an Impactful OSD

What is truly required is an Opportunity Scoping Document (OSD) that
resonates, communicates and impresses. The difference lies in the finesse
with which they are crafted. Here, we describe how to weave an OSD that
leaves a mark.

The Art of Reflection Over Regurgitation
Discovery sessions are incredibly valuable and packed with direct, unedited
insights. However, their real worth is not merely in recording what has been
said. It is in understanding the deeper needs, worries, and goals behind
these words. For PreSales, this means the OSD should not just be a word-
for-word record of the conversation. Rather, the key insights gathered
should be thoughtfully interpreted and summarised.

Consider a scenario where the prospect mentions, "We are struggling with
timely deliveries." A basic repetition would mean writing down this
statement exactly as it is. However, reflecting on this concern might lead
you to write, "The prospect is facing challenges in optimizing their delivery
process, leading to potential revenue loss and decreased client
satisfaction." The latter paints a clearer picture, showing that you have not
just heard but also understood the depth of the problem.

The Power of Visual Aids
Humans, by nature, are visual beings. Lengthy text can be overwhelming
and can sometimes cloud the main message that one aims to deliver. This
is where the visual aids come into play. You break monotony, simplify
complex ideas, and enhance retention. Visuals can make the OSD more
digestible and impactful, whether it is a flowchart illustrating the prospects
of an intricate supply chain or a table comparing the efficiencies of different
processes.

Imagine a prospective multistep procurement process. While you can use
paragraphs to detail each phase, a flowchart would allow the reader to

grasp the process complexities immediately. It is about making information
accessible, clear, and, most importantly, memorable.

Clarity is King
There is often the temptation to use complex jargon and technical terms.
However, simplicity is crucial in an OSD. The language should be clear,
direct, and concise. Every word and phrase needs to have a clear purpose,
ensuring that the document is easy to understand and accurately captures
the core of the discussion. (Greene 2018)

While industry-specific terminologies are essential for conveying certain
nuances, they should be used judiciously. Whenever they are used, ensure
that they are contextually relevant and well-understood by the prospect.
The aim is to communicate, not overwhelm or confuse.

Validation: The Seal of Agreement
Last but by no means least, an OSD, no matter how well crafted, holds little
value if it does not resonate with the prospects’ understanding and
expectations. Thus, before considering OSD as the final word, it is crucial to
have it validated by the prospect. You may not want to share the full OSD,
but you should validate the most crucial elements to ensure a common
understanding. This not only ensures alignment but also reinforces trust.
(Keenan 2018)

When a prospect sees its challenges, needs, and aspirations clearly and
concisely, it demonstrates a commitment to its part. When you have the
opportunity to validate or refine the content, it fosters collaboration,
making your prospect an active participant in the sales journey. (Raz 2017)

In conclusion, the OSD is not just another sales document; it is a narrative
of understanding and alignment, a bridge connecting a prospective
challenge to vendor solutions. Like any story worth its salt, its impact lies in
the telling itself. Through reflection, visualisation, clarity, and validation,
PreSales professionals can craft an OSD that is not just informative but truly
impactful, paving the way for successful engagement and lasting
relationships.


**Key Takeaway:**

Reflect, do not Regurgitate: Instead of merely repeating what was said
during discovery, interpret and present insights.

Use of Visual Aids: Incorporate diagrams, flowcharts, or tables where
complex processes or requirements can be simplified.

Prioritise Clarity: Use clear, concise language. Avoid jargon unless it is
industry-specific or relevant.

Validate with the Prospect: Before taking any further steps, ensure that
the prospect agrees with the content of the OSD.


### 8.4 Using the OSD Effectively

The OSD: A Beacon for Preparation
Each step in the sales process builds on the last step, creating a more
detailed and engaging story with the prospect. In this journey, the
Opportunity Scoping Document (OSD) acts as a crucial reminder. It is not
just about remembering specific details; it is about deeply understanding
the ongoing story of your interaction with your prospect.

By revisiting the OSD, you are not just refreshing your memory but also
realigning with the core challenges, aspirations, and nuances of the
prospect’s world. This alignment ensures that every solution is proposed,
every feature is highlighted, and every strategy discussed resonates deeply
with the prospective needs. It ensures continuity, coherence, and relevance
in the dialogue, reinforcing the perception of a vendor who truly "gets"
them.

Guiding Internal Strategy and Customisations
Beyond external engagement with prospects, the OSD has profound
internal significance. The OSD serves as the North Star within the
organisation, guiding various teams towards a unified goal.

Picture a situation where the product team plans custom features for the
prospect. The Opportunity Scoping Document (OSD) becomes a valuable
resource, offering documented insights that guide these decisions. This

ensures that any customisation closely aligns with the prospect-specific
challenges and needs. Similarly, when deciding which features to highlight
in a demo, the OSD acts as a guide, helping to focus on those aspects that
will most effectively demonstrate the potential impact and value of the
prospect.

Moreover, in internal strategy sessions, the OSD fosters a shared
understanding. Whether it is the marketing team crafting targeted
campaigns, the product team brainstorming feature enhancements, or the
sales team strategizing on upselling opportunities, the OSD ensures
everyone is harmoniously aligned with the prospect’s context.

Feedback: The Pulse of the Prospect Mind
While we put a lot of effort and precision into creating the OSD, it is
important to remember that it is not final. As our engagement with
prospect develops, our understanding of their needs and situations may
also change. Therefore, it is vital to regularly invite the prospect to review
the OSD and share feedback. This ensures that the document remains
relevant and accurately reflects the evolving nature of the engagement.
(Rosenberg 2015)

This feedback mechanism serves two purposes. First, it ensures that the
OSD remains updated and reflects the ongoing relationship. Nevertheless,
feedback provides a window into the prospects evolving priorities,
preferences, and decision-making processes. (Keenan 2018)

For instance, a prospect that emphasises a particular challenge signals its
growing significance. Similarly, a suggestion to explore a new area indicates
the potential expansion of the scope of engagement. These feedback
nuggets are goldmines, direct signals from the market that can inform not
just the current deal but also broader product and strategy decisions.

The Opportunity Scoping Document (OSD) is much more than just a static
record; it is a dynamic tool for engagement. For skilled PreSales
professionals, the OSD serves as a compass, a guiding light, and a way to
continually gauge progress. It helps navigate the path from initial
understanding to successful deal closures. Similar to any tool, its true

power lies in its use. When applied wisely, the OSD becomes a fundamental
part of successful, value-focused PreSales interactions.


**Key Takeaway:**

As a Preparation Tool: Before every subsequent engagement with the
prospect, review the OSD. This ensures that you are always aligned with the
prospects’ needs.

To Drive Internal Discussions: Within your team, the OSD can guide
product customisations, feature prioritisation, and demonstration
strategies.

As a Feedback Mechanism: Encourage prospects to provide feedback on
the OSD. Any changes or additions you suggest provide direct insight into
your priorities and decision-making processes.


### 8.5 Common Pitfalls and How to Avoid Them

This chapter will unravel some common missteps in the OSD crafting
process and explain strategies for cleverly bypassing them.

The Risk of the Generic Approach
In the diverse business world, no two prospects are identical. Each of them
has a unique set of challenges, aspirations, operational intricacies, and
cultural nuances. When creating an OSD, it is tempting to employ a one-
size-fits-all template, filling in blanks with prospect-specific details.
However, this approach runs the risk of creating a document that, although
technically accurate, lacks the depth and specificity required to truly
resonate with the prospect. (Hess 2020)

The key is customisation. A truly effective OSD is personalised and created
with careful attention to the specific characteristics of each prospect. It
delves beyond obvious issues, capturing the deeper motivations, concerns,
and goals of the prospect. By making sure the OSD resonates with the
prospect's own language and reflects their actual situation, PreSales
professionals can build a stronger relationship and show a real
understanding of their needs.

The Trap of Excessive Detail
There is a potential trap in the quest for thoroughness: Overloading the
OSD with an avalanche of detail. While it is natural to want to document
every single interaction, observation, and insight, doing so can dilute the
potency of the document. An OSD bloated with information can be
overwhelming, making it difficult for both the vendor and the prospect to
discern truly critical elements.

The key here is discernment. PreSales professionals must exercise
judgment when determining what should be included in the OSD. The focus
should be on the relevance and impact. Every piece of information should
pass a simple litmus test: Does it offer significant value in understanding
the prospect's challenges and aspirations? Otherwise, it might be best left
out or relegated to the appendix. By maintaining clarity and conciseness,
the OSD remains a sharp tool that effectively guides subsequent
engagements. (Keenan 2018)

The Oversight of Stagnation
The business landscape is dynamic, with constantly evolving needs,
challenges, and priorities. An OSD crafted at the onset of an engagement
may not remain wholly relevant as the relationship matures. A common
pitfall is treating the OSD as a static document, a snapshot in time, rather
than a living, evolving testament to the relationship.

To counteract this, PreSales professionals should adopt a proactive stance.
Periodic reviews of the OSD, especially before significant touchpoints with
the prospect, are essential. Moreover, feedback loops should be
established with the prospect, inviting them to offer updates, corrections,
or deeper insights. This ensures that the OSD remains current, reflecting
the most up-to-date understanding of the prospect’s world. By keeping the
OSD updated, it remains a trusted guide and steers engagement towards
successful outcomes.


**Key Takeaway:**

Being Overly Generic: Tailor the OSD specifically for each prospect. Avoid
using generic templates that do not resonate with the particular challenges
and nuances of the prospect.

Overloading with Information: While it is important to be thorough, avoid
the temptation to include every detail. Focus on what is most relevant and
impactful.

Not Keeping It Updated: As the engagement progresses and more is
understood about the prospect, ensure the OSD is updated to reflect these
insights.


> **Story**

Before we implemented the Opportunity Summary Document (OSD) into
our process, we struggled with inefficiencies and miscommunications that
led to significant internal conflicts and dissatisfaction from our clients.
Although we always had some form of an Opportunity Summary Document
or a summary of requirements, these documents often fell short of
providing the necessary details. This gap resulted in numerous pushbacks
from Professional Services and Product Management, who frequently
returned with a barrage of questions or pointed out missing critical
information.

The recurring issue was that our initial documentation failed to capture all
the essential information needed to move forward. Consequently, we were
caught in a frustrating cycle of internal conflicts. The Sales team felt
unsupported, Professional Services and Product Management were
overwhelmed with incomplete data, and ultimately, our clients grew
increasingly frustrated with the delays and confusion.

Realizing the need for a drastic change, we decided to start fresh. We
organized several internal sessions to dissect and clarify the specific
information required at each stage of the process. These sessions were
pivotal in identifying the key questions that needed answers and aligning
all departments on a standardized approach.

Through these collaborative efforts, we developed and implemented the
Opportunity Summary Document (OSD). This document became a
cornerstone of our process, ensuring that all necessary details were
captured comprehensively before moving forward.

With the OSD integrated into our workflow, the quality of our internal
communication improved significantly. The standardized format and

comprehensive nature of the OSD meant that when opportunities were
handed over, they came with all the relevant information, reducing the
back-and-forth and ensuring everyone was on the same page.

The impact was immediate and profound. Internal conflicts diminished as
Professional Services and Product Management received the thorough
information they needed to proceed efficiently. The Sales team felt more
supported, knowing that their efforts to gather and document
requirements were being effectively utilized. Most importantly, our clients
noticed the difference. They experienced smoother, more transparent
interactions with us, leading to greater satisfaction and trust.


## 9. Functional & Technical Qualification (FTQ)

In the complex PreSales landscape, professionals navigate through both
technical details and practical needs. This is where Functional & Technical
Qualification (FTQ) comes into play. The FTQ determines whether a
solution matches the prospective technical specifications and meets their
practical requirements. It is similar to finding the right piece for a jigsaw
puzzle, ensuring that it not only fits but also helps complete the overall
picture.
